Question Answer
If a state finds that it is impracticable to comply with an International Standard:it shall give immediate notice to ICAO of the differences between its own practices and the International Standard.
The JAA is controlled by:the JAA Committee.
The convention signed by the States and moved by a desire to endure adequate compensation for persons who suffer damage caused on the surface by foreign aircraft is:the Rome Convention.
The ICAO annex which deals with entry and departure of cargo and other articles on international flights is:Annex 9
To what did the Tokyo Convention of 1963 address itself?Interference with an aircraft in flight.
What is cabotage?Domestic air services by an operator within another State.
Who is responsible for the development and modifications of the SARPS?The ICAO Air Navigation Commission.
The convention on offences and certain acts committed on board aircraft is called:the Convention of Tokyo.
Which body of ICAO finalizes the Standard and Recommended Practices (SARPS) for submission for adoption?The Air Navigation Commission
The Chicago Convention was formed in:1944
The International Civil Aviation Organization (ICAO) was established by the international convention of:Warsaw
For which flights is the article about cabotage in the Convention of Chicago applicable?For domestic flights.
What does the second Freedom of the Air permit?To land for technical purposes (non commercial) in the territory of another State.
The Convention concerning the hijack of an aircraft is:the Tokyo Convention.
Which of the following is obligating for members of ICAO?ICAO must be informed about differences from the standards in any of the Annexes to the convention.
Annexes to the Chicago Convention contain:Standards and Recommended Practices
5th Freedom of the Air is:the right to carry revenue traffic between any points of landing on flights between 3 or more treaty partner nations (B to C to D).
Which is the permanent body of ICAO being responsible to the Assembly?The Council.
Annex 14 to the convention on international civil aviation contains SARPS for:aerodromes.
The Convention of Tokyo applies to damage:the above convention does not deal with this item.
What is cabotage?Limitation of domestic scheduled air services to a national carrier.
"""Cabotage"" refers to:"domestic air services.
The privilege to fly across the territory of another participating State without landing is called:the First Freedom of the Air.
The right to damages is lost if an action is not brought within:2 years.
Where was the Convention on International Civil Aviation signed in 1944?Chicago
The ICAO annex which deals with Rules of the Air is:Annex 2
A detailed description of the visual ground aids can be found in ICAO:Annex 14
Any contracting state may denounce the Convention of Tokyo by notification addressed to:International Civil Aviation Organisation.
Which freedom gives the privilege to land for non-traffic purposes in another ICAO Contracting State:the 4th Freedom.
An aircraft flying over the territory of another State must:follow the Rules of the air of the State it is overflying.
The privilege to land in another ICAO participating State for technical reasons is called:the Second Freedom.
The Warsaw Convention and later amendments deals with:limitation of the operator's liability for damage caused to passengers and goods transported.
Annex 17to the Convention of Chicago covers:Security
The Rome Convention and later amendments deal with:damage caused by foreign aircraft to third parties on the surface.
According to which Convention may an aircraft commander impose measures upon a person committing a crime or an offense on board the aircraft?The Convention of Warsaw.
ICAO personnel licensing rules and regulations are contained in Annex__to the Chicago Convention.1
Which of the following Annexes to the Chicago convention contains minimum specifications for a crew license to have international validity?Annex 1.
The objectives of ICAO were ratified by the:Chicago Convention 1944.
Which Freedom of the Air permits an aeroplane to land in a state for the purpose of refuelling?2nd Freedom.
Which of the following ICAO documents contain International Standards and Recommended Practices (SARPS)?Annexes to the Convention on international civil aviation.
The problems of hijacking were discussed at:the Tokyo Convention.
is Annex to the Convention on Civil Aviation."15
What can the commander of an aircraft do if he has reason to believe that a person has or is about to commit an offence in the aeroplane that is against penal law?All answers below are correct.
Any contracting state may denounce the Convention of Montreal by written notification to the depositary governments. The denunciation shall take effect:6 months following the date on which notification is received by the Depositary Governments.
Which convention on international air navigation resulted in the agreements concerning the responsibilities with illegal acts committed on board aircraft?The Tokyo Convention.
"The ""Standards"" contained in the Annexes to the Chicago convention are to be considered:"binding for the member States that have not notified ICAO about a national difference.
What is the obligation of a State in the event of non-compliance with an International Standard?The State has to publish such differences in the national AIP only.
Which Annex to the Chicago Convention covers dangerous goods carried in aircraft?Annex 18.
Article 36 of the Chicago Convention is concerned with photographic apparatus in aircraft. What rights does a state have with regard to article 36?The state may prohibit or regulate the use of photographic equipment in aircraft over its territory.
Concerning the Chicago Convention of 1944:each State has total sovereignty over the airspace above its territory.
The privilege of landing in another State for a technical stop only is called:the Second Freedom of the Air.
The Second Freedom of the Air is the:right to land for a technical stop.
The First Freedom of the Air is:the right to overfly without landing.
6th Freedom of the Air is:a combination of Freedoms 3 and 4. Revenue traffic flown between two treaty partner nations (C to A) through carriers base nation (B).
The president of the ICAO Council is elected for:3 years.
How will a member State withdraw from the Tokyo Convention?By informing ICAO.
"What privilege does the first ""Freedom of the Air"" grant?"Technical (non-commercial) landings in the territory of another State.
Which ICAO annex is dedicated to facilitate the passage of passengers at the aerodromes?Annex 9
What flights are protected by the Prevention of Terrorism Act?All flights.
Where there is an amendment to an International Standard a State must give notice to:the ICAO Council within 60 days of the adoption of the amendment.
One of the main objectives of ICAO is to:Develop principles and techniques for international aviation.
The International Civil Aviation Organization (ICAO) establishes:standards and recommended international practices for contracting member States.
Which convention deals with the unification of rules related to damage caused by aircraft to third parties on the surface?The Rome Convention.
An airline is planning a flight that will require a technical landing in a neighbouring State. Which Freedom of the Air will be exercised?2nd Freedom.
An aircraft having sustained damage while on the territory of a Contracting State other than the State of Registry may fly without fare-paying passengers to an airport at which it can be restored to an airworthy condition if:it receives permission of the State of Registry.
Annex 8 covers airworthiness of aircraft. Who is responsible for the administration of the Certificates of Airworthiness?The authority of the State of Registration.
Which of the following is not found on the Certificate of Airworthiness ?The name and address of the owner.
If an aeroplane is damaged the flight may be continued if:the State of Registry considers the aircraft to be airworthy even with the sustained damage.
The standards of Annex 8 - Part III (Airworthiness of Aircraft) relate to:aircraft with MTOM greater than 5.700 kg.
Who is responsible for determining the continuing airworthiness of an aeroplane?The State of Registry.
Who issues the Certificate of Airworthiness?The authority - State of Registration.
Who is competent to issue a Certificate of Airworthiness?The Contracting State which approves the aircraft on the basis of satisfactory evidence that the aircraft complies with appropriated airworthiness requirements.
Which of the following statements are correct concerning the flight crew compartment door?It must be capable of being locked.
Which of the following registration marks would not be permitted?SY-PAN
Which annex to the Chicago Convention deals with registration and marking of aircraft?Annex 7.
The Certificate of Registration shall:be carried on board the aircraft at all times.
A gyroplane is classified as a:rotorcraft.
The height of the marks under the wings of heavier-than-air aircraft shall be:at least 50 centimetres.
The height of the marks on lighter than air aircraft other than unmanned free balloons shall be:at least 50 centimetres.
The common mark shall be selected from the series of symbols included in the radio call signs allocated:to the International Civil Aviation Organisation by the International Telecommunication Union.
Which of the following letter groups may not be used as registration mark?PAN
A Certificate of Registration shall be kept___at all times.in the aircraft
Which of the following is not found on the Certificate of Registration?The category of aircraft.
According to Annex 7 (Aircraft Nationality and Registration Markings) certain combinations of letters are not to be used. These include:all of the above
When the first character of the registration mark is a letter:it may not be followed by a number.
Regarding an aircraft Certificate of Registration:aircraft can only be registered in one country.
The assignment of the common mark to a common mark registering authority will be made by:the International Civil Aviation Organisation.
Which of the following is a prohibited combination in aircraft registration letters?TTT
How high are the markings on the horizontal surfaces of an aeroplane?50 cm
The height of the marks on the fuselage (or equivalent structure) and on the vertical tail surfaces of heavier than air aircraft shall be:at least 30 centimetres.
ICAO Annex 7 contains:Standards but no recommended practices.
Annex 7 (Aircraft Nationality and Registration Marks) contains:standards only.
For which aircraft is MCC required?For multi-crew aeroplanes.
What is the maximum time period for which a JAR CPL licence can be issued?5 years.
In accordance with JAR-FCL 1 the credit for MPA co-pilot time is:100% of the co-pilot flight time towards the total flight time required for a higher grade of pilot licence.
Which of the statements concerning the privileges of a holder of a CPL(A) is correct?Act as PIC in commercial air transportation of any single-pilot aeroplane.
Type ratings are established for:each type of multi-pilot aeroplane (MPA).
A type rating is required for:any type of aircraft whenever considered necessary by the Licensing Authority.
What is the maximum period of validity if another ICAO Contracting State renders your licence valid?Valid to the expiry date on the licence.
When shall the holder of a medical certificate seek advice from an authorized medical examiner (AME)?Before the commencement of medical treatment.
To what matters does JAR-FCL-3 relate?Medical certificates.
In which circumstance does the holder of a medical certificate need to seek advice from the authority?Need for the regular use of correcting lenses.
What is the JAR-FCL definition of instrument time?Instrument flight time or instrument ground time.
A proficiency test took place on 15th April. Validity of last test was 30th June. The period for the next test can be up to but not exceed:31st of December the same year.
An applicant for a CPL aeroplane shall have completed in aeroplanes not less than:200 hours of flight time or 150 hours if completed during an integrated course of approved training organisation as a pilot of aeroplanes.
The duration of the period of currency of a medical assessment shall begin on the date:the medical assessment is issued.
The minimum age for a PPL shall be at least:17 years.
How old does an applicant have to be to hold a Commercial Pilot's Licence?18
What is the minimum age at which a flight instructor rating may be held?18
An applicant for a commercial pilot licence shall have completed in aeroplanes not less than:10 hours of instrument instruction time of which not more than 5 hours may be instrument ground time.
Type ratings shall be established:for any type of aircraft whenever considered necessary by the authority.
Before a flight instructor can instruct for the issue of CPL(A) he/she must have:500 hours as pilot of aeroplanes including 200 instructional hours.
The validity period of a PPL license for a pilot between 50 and 65 years is:1 year.
An applicant for a commercial pilot licence shall hold:a current class I medical assessment.
An applicant for a CPL(A) shall have completed at least the following flight time:150 hours if following an integrated course.
The minimum number of cross country hours needed for CPL(A) issue:20 hours cross country as PIC.
The holder of a pilot's licence should inform the Authority of any illness which they are suffering which involves incapacity to undertake those functions to which the licence relates throughout a period of a certain number of days or more. This number of days is:21
What is the maximum time period for which a pilot licence can be issued?5 years.
How is night defined?The hours between the end of evening civil twilight and the beginning of morning civil twilight.
How many classes of medical assessment are available for pilots?2
How long is a Class 1 medical certificate valid for?12 months if age below 40 and 6 months if above 40.
The holder of a pilot licence when acting as co-pilot performing under the supervision of the pilot-in-command the functions and duties of a pilot-in-command shall be entitled to a credit:in full with his flight time towards the total time required for higher grade of pilot licence.
The age of an applicant for a commercial pilot licence shall not be less than:18 years of age.
Medical requirements are contained in the following JAR-FCL Part:3
The validity period of a type rating is:one year.
For the issue of a CPL(A) what cross country experience is required?20 hours cross country as PIC including a cross country flight of at least 540 km (300 NM) during which 2 full stop landings at different aerodromes (other than the aerodrome of departure) are made.
The privileges of the holder of a commercial pilot licence - aeroplane shall be:to act as pilot-in-command in any aeroplane engaged in operations other than commercial air transportation.
An applicant for a commercial pilot licence aeroplane shall have completed in aeroplanes not less than:20 hours of cross-country flight time as pilot-in-command including a cross-country flight not less than 540 km (300 NM).
When should the holder of a medical certificate seek the advice of the authority or an AME?Any surgical operation or invasive medical procedure.
The minimum age for a CPL holder is:18 years.
The International Civil Aviation Convention Annex containing standards and recommended practices for Personnel Licensing is:Annex 1.
Who decides whether a type rating is considered necessary for any type of aircraft?The Licensing Authority.
You may act as a flight instructor to carry out flight instruction for the issue of a PPL:with a valid licence plus flight instructor rating.
How many hours or days would you have to spend in a clinic or hospital before you would have to inform the authorities?12 hours.
Which of the following correctly defines Special VFR?A flight cleared by ATC to operate within a CTR in conditions below VMC.
Where two aircraft are converging at the same level:the aircraft that has the other on its right shall give way.
If a pilot on a flight plan lands at an aerodrome other than his destination he must notify ATC of the destination aerodrome within___minutes of his planned ETA at destination.30
An aircraft is considered to overtake another if it approaches the other aircraft from the rear on a line forming an angle of less than:70 degrees with the plane of symmetry of the latter.
Series of red flashes directed towards an aircraft on ground mean:taxi clear of landing area in use.
A green intermittent light from aerodrome control to an aircraft on the ground means:taxi approved.
One of the following statements about aircraft ground movement is correct:A taxiing aircraft has priority over a vehicle towing an aircraft.
On aerodromes aircraft taxiing on the manoeuvring area of an aerodrome shall give way to:aircraft taking off or about to take off.
"The light signal indicating ""give way to other aircraft and continue circling"" is:"steady red.
The person who has final authority as to the disposition of an aircraft during flight time is:the commander.
A flight plan shall be submitted prior to departure for a controlled flight at least:60 minutes prior to departure.
A flight plan shall be submitted for:any flight across an international boundary.
A controlled flight is requested to inform the appropriate ATC unit whenever the average True Air Speed at cruis¬ing level varies or is expected to vary from that given in the flight plan by plus or minus:5%
An aircraft is at 12.000 ft in category F airspace (VFR). The required distance from cloud is:1.500 m horizontal and 1.000 ft vertical.
"Aircraft ""A "" with an ATC clearance is flying in VMC conditions within a control area. Aircraft ""B"" with no ATC clearance is approaching at approximately the same altitude and on a converging course. Which has the right of way?""Aircraft ""B"" if ""A"" is on its left."
VFR flights shall not be operated under which of the following conditions? 1) Above FL200 2) At transonic and supersonic speedsBoth statements are correct.
"What is meant by the term ""total EET"" for a VFR flight?"Time from takeoff to overhead the airfield.
An aircraft manoeuvring in an airport's circuit receives a series of red flashes from the control tower. This signifies that the aircraft must:not land because the airport is not available for landing.
At night you observe ground signals from survivors of a disaster. What do you do to indicate that you have seen and understood the signals?Flash you landing lights or navigation lights.
What is Special VFR?A VFR flight cleared by ATC to operate within a CTR in meteorological conditions below VMC.
What is a danger area?An airspace of defined dimensions within which activities dangerous to the flight of aircraft may exist at specified times.
An ETA for an IFR flight refers to the following:IAF
You have filed a VFR flight plan. What do you put in field 16 (total estimated elapsed time)?Time from takeoff to overhead the destination.
A marshaller has his arms fully extended above his head with wands pointing up. This means that:you should proceed to this bay.
Aircraft on the manoeuvring area have to give way to:aircraft landing and taking off.
A flashing intermittent red light from the ground to an aircraft in the air means:continue for another approach.
An aircraft is coming in from the left. Which light will you see first?Steady green.
"Which signal from a marshaller indicates ""all clear""?"Right arm raised bent at elbow with thumb extended.
When is deviation from the Rules of the Air permitted?Only in the interests of flight safety.
Who is charged with the safe conduct of a flight?The PIC.
How is ground visibility defined?The visibility at an aerodrome as reported by an accredited observer or by automatic systems.
Which of the following defines flight visibility?The forward visibility from the cockpit of an aircraft in flight.
In class D airspace the minimum flight visibility for VFR flight above FL 100 is:8 km
"The VMC minima for an airspace classified as ""G"" above 10.000 feet MSL are:"1.500 m horizontally and 1.000 feet vertically from clouds; 8 km visibility.
Who shall have the final authority over the disposition of the aircraft?The commander.
Anti-collision lights on an aircraft must be switched on:between SS and SR or any other period specified by the appropriate authority.
The highest priority for landing has:an aircraft that is compelled to land (Emergency landing).
"What signal from a marshaller to a pilot indicates ""apply brakes""?"Clenching a raised fist.
A series of green flashes from aerodrome control directed towards an aircraft on ground means:cleared to taxi.
Whilst airborne you see a flashing green light from the tower. What does this mean?Return for landing and await clearance to land.
What is the meaning of AGL?Above ground level.
What is the minimum flight altitude permitted over towns and settlements and populated areas?The altitude which permits the aircraft to land safely in the event of an engine failure.
Flight visibility is:the visibility forward from the flight deck of an aircraft in flight.
"Which signal to an aircraft in flight means ""return for landing""?"A series of green flashes.
Deviation from the TAS in the flight plan is to be reported to ATC. By how much would the TAS have to deviate before it is reported?5%
You are flying at 5.000 ft (above the transition altitude) in class C airspace. What are the VMC criteria?5 km visibility: 1.000 ft vertically and 1.500 m horizontally clear of cloud.
A flashing intermittent red light from the ground to an aircraft on the ground means:clear the landing area.
What does a red flashing light from the control tower to an aircraft on the manoeuvring area mean?Move clear of the landing area.
Your aircraft is intercepted by a military aircraft. The signals given by this aircraft conflict with ATC instructions. You should:follow the instructions of the intercepting aircraft.
Transition altitude is defined as:the altitude at or below which the vertical position of aircraft is expressed in reference to mean sea level.
To what do the ICAO Rules of the Air (Annex 2) apply in general?Both A) and B) are correct.
Aircraft taxiing in the manoeuvring area must give way to:departing and landing traffic.
An airborne flight plan must be submitted:10 minutes before the intended point of entry into a CTA or advisory area.
Which of the following flights has the greatest priority to land?Emergency aircraft.
Pilots of controlled flights are requested to inform the appropriate ATS whenever the average TAS at cruising level between reporting points varies or is expected to vary from the TAS given in the flight plan by:5%
Which of the following correctly defines flight visibility?The visibility forward from the cockpit of an aeroplane in flight.
"Which manoeuvre shall be executed by an intercepting aircraft if the pilot wants to communicate to the intercepted aircraft ""YOU MAY PROCEED""?"Executing a climbing turn of 90 degrees or more without crossing the line of flight of the intercepted aircraft.
What is aerodrome traffic?All traffic on the manoeuvring area of an aerodrome and flying in the vicinity of the aerodrome.
A steady green light from aerodrome control to an aircraft on the ground means:cleared for takeoff.
A special VFR clearance may be obtained from ATC for the following airspaces:CTR
What defines a danger area?Airspace of defined dimension where activities dangerous to flight may exist.
While taxiing an aircraft receives the following light signal from the control tower: series of red flashes. This signal means that the aircraft:must vacate the landing area in use.
SVFR may be authorized when the ground visibility is not less than:1.500 m
Aircraft shall not be flown in formation except:by pre-arrangement among the PICs taking part and if the flight is to be in CAS in accordance with the conditions laid out by ICAO Annex 2 and supplemented by the national procedures.
A series of green flashes from aerodrome control directed towards an aircraft in flight means:return for landing.
You have been given clearance by ATC but you are suddenly forced to deviate from it for some reason. You should:inform ATC as soon as possible about the deviation.
Which of the following actions shall be taken in case a controlled flight deviates from the track?Adjust the heading of aircraft to regain track as soon as practicable.
The visual signal for indicating a state of distress is:a succession of red pyrotechnics.
The appropriate ATS unit has to be informed:if the average TAS at cruising level varies or is expected to vary by ±5% from that given in the flight plan.
When two taxiing aircraft are converging:the one that has the other on its right gives way.
The transition level:shall be the lowest available flight level above the transition altitude that has been established.
When should the QNH be communicated to aircraft prior to takeoff?When taxi clearance is given.
When must you operate your SSR transponder?At all times unless otherwise instructed by ATC.
At what moment during the approach should the reported airfield altimeter setting be set?When passing the transition level.
The vertical position of an aircraft at or above the transition level will be reported:as flight level.
Pilots shall not squawk IDENT unless they:are requested by ATC.
"Minimum height for ""Transition Altitude"" over an airfield shall be:"3.000 ft
In the standard atmosphere FL35 is equivalent to:1.050 metres.
An aircraft is in controlled airspace under ATC control. The responsibility for ensuring adequate terrain clearance rests with:the aircraft commander.
What will be the transponder mode and code for radio communication failure?Mode A code 7600.
When must Mode C be switched on?Continuously unless otherwise directed by ATC.
Which of the following correctly defines the NOZ for parallel runway operations?The NOZ extends from runway threshold to the point where aircraft are normally established on the localiser.
When shall the SQUAWK IDENT button be pushed by the pilot?Only if requested by ATC.
An aircraft equipped with an SSR transponder is expected to operate the transponder on Mode A code to indicate specifically that it is subjected to unlawful interference.7500
What SSR code indicates communications failure?7600
Independent parallel approaches may be conducted to parallel runways provided that a No Transgression Zone/ NTZ is established equidistant between the extended runway centre lines:610 m
During flight through the transition layer the vertical position of the aircraft should be expressed as:altitude above mean sea level during descent.
"Which code shall be used on mode ""A"" to provide recognition of an emergency aircraft?"Code 7700.
The vertical position of an aircraft at or below the transition altitude will be reported:as altitude.
Pilots shall not operate the SSR special position indicator (IDENT) feature unless:requested by ATC.
The transition level:is calculated by ATS.
Which of the following correctly lists special purpose codes that are to be used in conjunction with Secondary Surveillance Radar (SSR)?Distress 7700; Hijacking 7500; Communication failure 7600.
Which of the following defines transition altitude (TA)?The altitude at which 1.013 mb is set and vertical position above TA then reported as a flight level.
The vertical position of an aircraft is expressed as altitude when:the aircraft is at or below the transition altitude.
A pre-flight altimeter check should be carried out:at a known elevation on the aerodrome.
The NTZ extends from___to___.the threshold of the nearer runway; the point at which 1.000 ft vertical separation is reduced between aircraft
The SSR code to indicate communications failure is:A7600+C
A pilot should set a flight level on departure:at the transition altitude.
In the vicinity of an aerodrome that is going to be used by the aircraft the vertical position of the aircraft shall be expressed in:altitude above sea level on or below the transition altitude.
In the standard atmosphere FL150 is equivalent to:4.550 metres.
The transition altitude of an aerodrome should not be below:3.000 ft.
The pilot of an aircraft losing two-way communications shall set the transponder to Mode A Code:7600
Which of the following transponder codes is not a valid SSR mode A squawk?A5678
If a transponder failure is detected before departure from an aerodrome the aircraft:can fly to an aerodrome where the transponder can be repaired.
Flight above the transition altitude is referenced to:flight levels when 1.013 hPa is set.
The pilot must fly heading:"030° magnetic.
What is the speed limit in class E airspace?250 kts below FL100.
"When IFR flights are cleared to fly maintaining own separation while in VMCthe following shall apply:
1) The clearance shall be for a specified portion of the flight at or below 10.000 ftduring climb or descent.
In which class(es) of airspace can you fly VFR without a radio?E
Approach Control has the following duties:inform aircraft if the approach delay is greater than 30 minutes.
A separation minimum shall be applied between a LIGHT or MEDIUM aircraft and a HEAVY aircraft and between a LIGHT aircraft and a MEDIUM aircraft when the heavier aircraft is making a low or missed approach and the lighter aircraft is landing on the same runway in the opposite direction or on a parallel opposite direction runway sepa¬rated by:less than 760 m.
Which procedure you follow if during an IFR flight in VMC you have two-way communication failure?Continue the flight maintaining VMC and land as soon as practicable.
When are ATIS broadcasts updated?Upon receipt of information of a significant change in weather conditions.
Which of the following is an objective of Air Traffic Services?To expedite and maintain an orderly flow of traffic.
Under which circumstances may a pilot deviate from a published instrument approach procedure?If visual reference is established before the completion of the instrument approach procedure and the aircraft is cleared for a visual approach.
The Alerting Service is provided by:the ATS unit responsible for the aircraft at that moment.
When shall an ATIS broadcast be updated?Immediately when a significant change occurs.
An aircraft captain should transmit special aircraft observations when he encounters:all of the above.
Which phase of emergency is declared if an aircraft is known or believed to be the subject of unlawful interference?ALERFA.
Does an ATC clearance always include prevention of collision with terrain?Only when the aircraft is being radar vectored.
An Expected Approach Time (EAT) will be transmitted by the most expeditious means to the aircraft when it is expected that it has to hold:for 30 minutes or more.
"Which suffix would be added to an airway designator to indicate that turns between 30"" and 90° below FL200 shall be made within the allowable tolerance of a tangential arc between straight leg segments with a minimum radius of 15 NM?"Z
The following minimum radar separation shall be provided between aircraft on the same localizer (at any distance from the runway threshold) with additional longitudinal separation as required for wake turbulence:3NM
An Air Traffic Control Service will be provided in which of the following?To all Special VFR flights.
A pilot receiving an IFR clearance from ATC should:read back the entire clearance as required by regulation.
IFR clearance is always valid:to the clearance limit.
Where can an ACC issue a clearance to controlled flights operating in VMC to maintain own clearance subject to maintaining VMC and own separation?Only in airspace class D and E.
What is the speed limit in class E airspace?250 kts IAS for IFR and VFR below FL100.
With reference to wake turbulence - what is the minimum separation of LIGHT aircraft landing after a HEAVY aircraft?6NM
For a timed approach the following minima should be observed:The spacing for a MEDIUM aircraft behind a HEAVY aircraft is 2 minutes.
A lower limit of a Control Area shall be established at a height above the ground level or water of not less than:200 metres.
"The letter ""L"" is written in the wake turbulence box of a flight plan form when the maximum certified takeoff weight of an aircraft is less than or equal to:"7.000 kg.
The Takeoff Mass of MEDIUM aircraft is as follows:less than 136.000 kg but more than 7.000 kg.
"When should the word ""HEAVY"" be included as a suffix to the call sign?"On the initial call to ATC if certified MTOM exceeds 136.000 kg.
What is the correct content of 'essential traffic' information messages to aircraft?Direction; type; level; ETA over the relevant reporting point.
When should position reports be made?When passing each designated compulsory reporting point.
What is the maximum delay that can be accepted before a new or amended flight plan is to be filed (assume uncontrolled flight)?60 minutes.
The width of an advisory route is:10 NM
One of the functions ensured by a radar control unit for the provision of approach control service is:to conduct surveillance radar approaches.
3) As the ACAS capability of an aircraft is known to ATCpilots may be required to maintain their own separation in cruise.
When does Air Traffic Control Services have the responsibility to prevent collisions with terrain?When a flight in accordance with IFR is vectored by radar.
Regarding Aerodrome Flight Information Service (AFIS):it can only supply limited services to the users and under no circumstances may it supply ATC services.
Which of the following statements describes the Alert Phase (ALERFA)?An aircraft which has been cleared to land fails to land within 5 minutes of the ETA and communication has not been re-established.
Secondary Surveillance Radar (SSR) is not available. For radar identification ATC may request the pilot to execute one or more heading changes of:30° or more
ATC clocks are checked to ensure that the time is correct to within:± 30 seconds.
Essential traffic is:controlled traffic not separated from another controlled traffic with the prescribed separation minima.
A pilot encountering windshear should report the fact to ATC:as soon as possible.
"What is the definition of ""aerodrome traffic""?"Traffic on the manoeuvring area and in the local vicinity of the aerodrome.
Air traffic services unit clocks and other time recording devices shall be checked as necessary to ensure correct time to within plus or minus:30 seconds of UTC at all times.
An Expected Approach Time (EAT) is given:when an aircraft is instructed to hold.
Clearance to land or any alternative clearance received from the non-radar controller should normally be passed to the aircraft before it reaches a distance of:2 NM from touchdown.
What is the objective of filing an ATIR (Air Traffic Incident Report)?To promote aircraft flight safety.
What is the maximum speed adjustment that a pilot should be requested to make when under radar control and established on intermediate and final approach?±20 kts
Except otherwise established by the appropriate ATS authority a Surveillance Radar Approach (SRA) shall be terminated at a distance from the touchdown of:2NM
Cruising level IFR during cruise within controlled airspace shall be given as flight level (FL):above the transition altitude when applicable.
Runway Visual Range is reported and passed to an aircraft when the visibility falls below:1.500 m.
Which of the following statements regarding Alerting service is correct?Alerting Service and Flight Information Service are often provided by the same ATS unit.
What is the correct content of a position report?Aircraft ident; position; time; FL or alt; next position; ETA; ensuing position.
FIS:provides advice and information useful for the safe and efficient conduct of flight.

"Conical probe is another type of AofA sensor. It is a ""tube"" that extends perpendicularly from the fuselage into the free airflow along the fuselage. Inside the fuselage the probe is attached to a paddle- wheel and this entire assembly (probe + wheel) are free to rotate along their axis. The probe has two slots along its lengthallowing airflow to pass inside the probe and then routed onto each side of the paddle wheel. Variations in the airflow direction (angle of attack changes) cause pressure changes in the probe and subsequently change the position of the paddle wheel. Position of the paddle wheel then determines the Angle of Attack.

On an IFR flight two-way communication is lost as the aircraft is holding above the final destination. The expected approach time (EAT) was passed as 1420 UTC before communication was lost. The aircraft should squawk 7600 and make an approach to land at:not before the EAT and no later than 30 minutes after EAT.

A departing aircraft experiencing radio communication failure on an IFR flight under radar vectors has to:squawk 7600 and thereafter return to the route indicated in the current flight plan in the most direct manner.
